### SMC: Compare scan matrix (S7-1500)

#### Description

You can use the "Compare scan matrix" instruction to compare the signal state of up to 16 programmed input bits (IN_BIT0 to IN_BIT15) with the corresponding bit of the comparison masks for each step. Processing starts at step 1 and is continued until the last programmed step (LAST) or until a match is found. The input bit of the IN_BIT0 parameter is compared with the value of the mask CMP_VAL[x,0], with "x" indicating the step number. All programmed values are compared in the same manner. If a match is found the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "1" and the step number with the matching mask is written in the OUT_STEP parameter. Unprogrammed input bits or unprogrammed bits of the mask have a default signal state FALSE. If more than one step has a matching mask, only the first one found is indicated in the OUT_STEP parameter. If no match is found, the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "0". In this case the value at the OUT_STEP parameter is greater by "1" than the value at the LAST parameter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Compare scan matrix" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN_BIT0 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 0 is compared with bit 0 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT1 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 1 is compared with bit 1 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT2 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 2 is compared with bit 2 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT3 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 3 is compared with bit 3 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT4 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 4 is compared with bit 4 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT5 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 5 is compared with bit 5 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT6 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 6 is compared with bit 6 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT7 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 7 is compared with bit 7 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT8 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 8 is compared with bit 8 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT9 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 9 is compared with bit 9 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT10 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 10 is compared with bit 10 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT11 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 11 is compared with bit 11 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT12 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 12 is compared with bit 12 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT13 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 13 is compared with bit 13 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT14 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 14 is compared with bit 14 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT15 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Input bit 15 is compared with bit 15 of the mask. |
| OUT | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates that a match was found.  A signal state of "0" indicates that no match was found. |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| OUT_STEP | Output | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Contains the step number with the matching mask or the step number which is greater by "1" than the value of the LAST parameter, provided no match is found. |
| LAST | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Specifies the step number of the last step to be scanned for a matching mask. |
| CMP_VAL | Static | ARRAY OF WORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Comparison masks [0 to 15, 0 to 15]: The first number of the index is the step number and the second number is the bit number of the mask. |

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 000E | The value at the LAST parameter is greater than 15. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

#### Example

In this example, all 16 input bits are compared with the mask for steps 0 through 5 until a match is found. Only the masks for steps 0 through 2 are scanned, since the mask for step 2 matches the input bit.

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL SMC, "SMC_DB" | // The "Compare scan matrix" instruction is called and the instance data block "SMC_DB" is created. |
| IN_BIT0 := "Tag_Input_BIT0" | // Input bit 0 |
| IN_BIT1 := "Tag_Input_BIT1" | // Input bit 1 |
| IN_BIT2 := "Tag_Input_BIT2" | // Input bit 2 |
| IN_BIT3 := "Tag_Input_BIT3" | // Input bit 3 |
| IN_BIT4 := "Tag_Input_BIT4" | // Input bit 4 |
| IN_BIT5 := "Tag_Input_BIT5" | // Input bit 5 |
| IN_BIT6 := "Tag_Input_BIT6" | // Input bit 6 |
| IN_BIT7 := "Tag_Input_BIT7" | // Input bit 7 |
| IN_BIT8 := "Tag_Input_BIT8" | // Input bit 8 |
| IN_BIT9 := "Tag_Input_BIT9" | // Input bit 9 |
| IN_BIT10 := "Tag_Input_BIT10" | // Input bit 10 |
| IN_BIT11 := "Tag_Input_BIT11" | // Input bit 11 |
| IN_BIT12 := "Tag_Input_BIT12" | // Input bit 12 |
| IN_BIT13 := "Tag_Input_BIT13" | // Input bit 13 |
| IN_BIT14 := "Tag_Input_BIT14" | // Input bit 14 |
| IN_BIT15 := "Tag_Input_BIT15" | // Input bit 15 |
| OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Indicates whether or not a match was found. |
| OUT_STEP := "Tag_Output_STEP" | // Contains the step number with the relevant mask. |
| ERR_CODE := "Tag_ErrorCode" | // Error information |

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

#### Before processing

In this example, the following values are used for the input and output parameters:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN_BIT0 | Tag_Input_BIT0 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT1 | Tag_Input_BIT1 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT2 | Tag_Input_BIT2 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT3 | Tag_Input_BIT3 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT4 | Tag_Input_BIT4 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT5 | Tag_Input_BIT5 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT6 | Tag_Input_BIT6 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT7 | Tag_Input_BIT7 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT8 | Tag_Input_BIT8 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT9 | Tag_Input_BIT9 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT10 | Tag_Input_BIT10 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT11 | Tag_Input_BIT11 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT12 | Tag_Input_BIT12 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT13 | Tag_Input_BIT13 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT14 | Tag_Input_BIT14 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT15 | Tag_Input_BIT15 | TRUE |
| OUT | Tag_Output | FALSE |
| OUT_STEP | Tag_Output_STEP | B#16#00 |
| ERR_CODE | Tag_ErrorCode | W#16#0000 |

The following values for the mask of step 2 are saved in the instance data block "SMC_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| CMP_VAL [2,0] | DBX12.0 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,1] | DBX12.1 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,2] | DBX12.2 | FALSE |
| CMP_VAL [2,3] | DBX12.3 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,4] | DBX12.4 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,5] | DBX12.5 | FALSE |
| CMP_VAL [2,6] | DBX12.6 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,7] | DBX12.7 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,8] | DBX13.0 | FALSE |
| CMP_VAL [2,0] | DBX13.1 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,10] | DBX13.2 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,11] | DBX13.3 | FALSE |
| CMP_VAL [2,12] | DBX13.4 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,13] | DBX13.5 | TRUE |
| CMP_VAL [2,14] | DBX13.6 | FALSE |
| CMP_VAL [2,15] | DBX13.7 | TRUE |
| LAST | DB84 | B#16#05 |

#### After processing

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| OUT | Tag_Output | TRUE |
| OUT_STEP | Tag_Output_STEP | B#16#02 |
| ERR_CODE | Tag_ErrorCode | W#16#0000 |

### LEAD_LAG: Lead and lag algorithm  (S7-1500)

#### Description

You can use the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction to process signals with an analog tag. The gain value at the GAIN parameter must be greater than zero. The result of the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction is calculated using the following equation:

![Description](images/49016018315_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction supplies plausible results only when processing is in fixed program cycles. The same units must be specified at the parameters LD_TIME, LG_TIME and SAMPLE_T. At LG_TIME &gt; 4 + SAMPLE_T, the instruction approaches the following function:

OUT = GAIN * ((1 + LD_TIME * s) / (1 + LG_TIME * s)) * IN

When the value of the GAIN parameter is less than or equal to zero, the calculation is not performed and an error information is output on the ERR_CODE parameter.

You can use the instruction "Lead and lag algorithm" in conjunction with loops as a compensator in dynamic feed-forward control. The instruction consists of two operations. The "Lead" operation shifts the phase of the OUT output so that the output leads the input. The "Lag" operation, on the other hand, shifts the output so that the output lags behind the input. Because the "Lag" operation is equivalent to an integration, it can be used as a noise suppressor or as a low-pass filter. The "Lead" operation is equivalent to a differentiation and can therefore be used as a high-pass filter. The two instructions together (Lead and Lag) result in the output phase lagging behind the input at lower frequencies and leading it at higher frequencies. This means that the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction can be used as a band pass filter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | The input value of the current sample time (cycle time) to be processed |
| SAMPLE_T | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Sample time |
| OUT | Output | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| LD_TIME | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Lead time in the same unit as sample time. |
| LG_TIME | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Lag time in the same unit as sample time |
| GAIN | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Gain as % / % (the ratio of the change in output to a change in input as a steady state). |
| PREV_IN | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Previous input |
| PREV_OUT | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Previous output |

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 0009 | The value at the GAIN parameter is less than or equal to zero. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL LEAD_LAG, "LEAD_LAG_DB" | // The "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction is called and the instance data block "LEAD_LAG_DB" is created. |
| IN := "Tag_Input" | // The input value of the current sample time (cycle time) to be processed. |
| SAMPLE_T := "Tag_Input_SAMPE_T" | // Sample time |
| OUT := "Tag_Output_Result" | // Result of the instruction |
| ERR_CODE := "Tag_ErrorCode" | // Error information |

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

#### Before processing

In this example the following values are used for the input parameters:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_Input | 2.0 |
| SAMPLE_T | Tag_InputSampleTime | 10 |

The following values are saved in the "LEAD_LAG_DB" instance data block of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| LD_TIME | DBD12 | 2.0 |
| LG_TIME | DBD16 | 2.0 |
| GAIN | DBD20 | 1.0 |
| PREV_IN | DBD24 | 6.0 |
| PREV_OUT | DBD28 | 6.0 |

#### After processing

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| OUT | Tag_Output_Result | 2.0 |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "LEAD_LAD_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| PREV_IN | DBD24 | 2.0 |
| PREV_OUT | DBD28 | 2.0 |

### SEG: Create bit pattern for seven-segment display (S7-1500)

#### Description

The "Create bit pattern for seven-segment display" instruction converts each of the four hexadecimal digits in the specified source word (IN) into four equivalent codes for a 7-segment display and writes these to the double word of the output (OUT).

The "Create bit pattern for seven-segment display" does not recognize any error conditions.

The relationship between the input hexadecimal values and the output bit patterns is as follows:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Digit** | **‑gfedcba** | **Display** |  |
| 0000 | 00111111 | 0 |  |
| 0001 | 00000110 | 1 |  |
| 0010 | 01011011 | 2 | Seven-segment display |
| 0011 | 01001111 | 3 | ![Description](images/7307290891_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png) |
| 0100 | 01100110 | 4 |  |
| 0101 | 01101101 | 5 |  |
| 0110 | 01111101 | 6 |  |
| 0111 | 00000111 | 7 |  |
| 1000 | 01111111 | 8 |  |
| 1001 | 01100111 | 9 |  |
| 1010 | 01110111 | A |  |
| 1011 | 01111100 | B |  |
| 1100 | 00111001 | C |  |
| 1101 | 01011110 | D |  |
| 1110 | 01111001 | E |  |
| 1111 | 01110001 | F |  |

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Create bit pattern for seven-segment display" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | IN | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Source word with four hexadecimal digits. |
| OUT | OUT | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Destination bit pattern with four bytes. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL SEG | // The "Create bit pattern for seven-segment display" instruction is called. |
| IN := "Tag_Input" | // Source word |
| OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Bit pattern for the seven-segment display |

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Hexadecimal | Binary |  |  |
| IN | Tag_Input | W#16#1234 | 0001 0010 0011 0100 |
| OUT | Tag_Output | DW#16#065B4F66 | 00000110 01011011 01001111 01100110  Display: 1234 |

---

### BCDCPL: Create tens complement (S7-1500)

#### Description

The "Create tens complement" instruction is used to create the tens complement of a seven-digit BCD number specified by the IN parameter. This instruction uses the following mathematical formula to calculate:

10000000 (as BCD)

– 7-digit BCD value

----------------------------------------

Tens complement (as BCD)

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Create tens complement" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Input | Bit strings | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | 7-digit BCD number |
| ERR_CODE | Output | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL BCDCPL | // The instruction is called. |
| IN := "Tag_Input" | // 7-digit BCD number |
| ERR_CODE := "Tag_Output" | // Tens complement of the specified BCD number |

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value* |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_Input | DW#16#01234567 |
| ERR_CODE | Tag_Output | DW#16#08765433 |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |  |

### BITSUM: Count number of set bits (S7-1500)

#### Description

The "Count number of set bits" instruction is used to count the number of bits of an operand that is set to the signal state "1". The operand whose bits are to be counted is specified on the IN parameter. The result of the instruction is output at the RET_VAL parameter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Count number of set bits" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Input | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Operand whose set bits are counted |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Number of set bits |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL BITSUM | // The instruction is called. |
| IN := "Tag_Input" | // Operand whose set bits are counted. |
| RET_VAL := "Tag_Output" | // Number of set bits of the operand "Tag_Input". |

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value* |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_Input | DW#16#12345678 |
| RET_VAL | Tag_Output | W#16#000D (13 bits) |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |  |

This section contains information on the following topics:

#### A: AND logic operation (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "AND logic operation" to query whether the signal state of a binary operand is "1" and to AND the query result with the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The query result is hereby identical with the signal state of the checked operand.

After execution of the instruction the RLO will be "1" if both linked signal states are also "1". If one of the linked signal states is "0", the RLO is "0" after executing the instruction.

If you use the instruction multiple times consecutively, all query results must be "1" for the common result of the logic operation to also be "1".

You can also use the instruction "AND logic operation" to query the signal state of the status word. To do this, specify the relevant status bit (==0, &lt;&gt;0, &gt;0, &lt;0, &gt;=0, &lt;=0, OV, OS, UO, BR) as parameter of the instruction.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "AND logic operation" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Operand whose signal state is queried. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19218917899_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

---

#### AN: Negated AND logic operation (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "Negated AND logic operation" to query whether the signal state of a binary operand is "0" and to AND the query result with the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The result of the query is hereby the negated signal state of the checked operand. If the operand has signal state "0," the result of the query is "1". If the operand has signal state "1," the result of the query is "0".

After the instruction executes, the RLO is "1" if the result of the query and the RLO before the execution of the instruction have signal state "1".

After the instruction executes, the RLO is "0" if the result of the query or the RLO before the execution of the instruction have signal state "0".

You can also use the instruction "Negated AND logic operation" to query the signal state of the status word. To do this, specify the relevant status bit (==0, &lt;&gt;0, &gt;0, &lt;0, &gt;=0, &lt;=0, OV, OS, UO, BR) as parameter of the instruction.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Negated AND logic operation" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Operand whose signal state is queried. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19218922251_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### O: OR logic operation (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "OR logic operation" to query whether the signal state of a binary operand is "1" and to OR the query result with the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The query result is hereby identical with the signal state of the checked operand.

After the instruction executes, the RLO is "1" if one of the linked signal states is "1". If both linked signal states are "0", the RLO is "0" after the instruction executes.

If you use the instruction multiple times consecutively, it is sufficient that one of the results of the query is "1" for the common result of the logic operation to also be "1".

You can also use the instruction "OR logic operation" to query the signal state of the status word. To do this, specify the relevant status bit (==0, &lt;&gt;0, &gt;0, &lt;0, &gt;=0, &lt;=0, OV, OS, UO, BR) as parameter of the instruction.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "OR logic operation" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Operand whose signal state is queried. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19218980875_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### ON: Negated OR logic operation (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "Negated OR logic operation" to query whether the signal state of a binary operand is "0" and to OR the query result with the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The result of the query is hereby the negated signal state of the checked operand. If the operand has signal state "0," the result of the query is "1". If the operand has signal state "1," the result of the query is "0".

After the instruction executes, the RLO is "1" if the result of the query or the RLO before the execution of the instruction have signal state "1". If both linked signal states are "0", the RLO is also "0" after the instruction executes.

If you use the instruction multiple times consecutively, it is sufficient that one of the results of the query is "1" for the common result of the logic operation to also be "1".

You can also use the instruction "Negated OR logic operation" to query the signal state of the status word. To do this, specify the relevant status bit (==0, &lt;&gt;0, &gt;0, &lt;0, &gt;=0, &lt;=0, OV, OS, UO, BR) as parameter of the instruction.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Negated OR logic operation" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Operand whose signal state is checked |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/44976676619_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### X: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" to query whether the signal state of a binary operand is "1" and to XOR the query result with the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The query result is hereby identical with the signal state of the checked operand. After the instruction EXECUTES, the RLO is "1" if the linked signal states are not equal. The RLO is "0" if both signal states are the same.

If, for example, the RLO before execution of the instruction is "1" and the queried operand is "1", the RLO is reset to "0". If the RLO is "1" and the operand has signal state "0", the RLO is set to "1" after the instruction executes.

If you use the instruction several times consecutively, it is sufficient that one of the query results is "1" for the common RLO to be "1" as well. If all query results are "1" or "0" the RLO is reset to "0".

You can also use the instruction "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" to query the signal state of the status word. To do this, specify the relevant status bit (==0, &lt;&gt;0, &gt;0, &lt;0, &gt;=0, &lt;=0, OV, OS, UO, BR) as parameter of the instruction.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Operand whose signal state is queried. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19219110923_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### XN: Negated EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Negated EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" instruction to query whether the signal state of a binary operand is "0" and to OR the query result with the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The result of the query is hereby the negated signal state of the checked operand. After the instruction EXECUTES, the RLO is "1" if the linked signal states are not equal. The RLO is "0" if both signal states are the same.

If, for example, the queried operand has signal state "0," the result of the query is "1". XORing the query result with an RLO "1" results in signal state "0". The logic operation with an RLO "0" results in signal state "1".

You can also use the "Negated EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" instruction to query the signal state of the status word. To do this, specify the relevant status bit (==0, &lt;&gt;0, &gt;0, &lt;0, &gt;=0, &lt;=0, OV, OS, UO, BR) as parameter of the instruction.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Negated EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Operand whose signal state is queried. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19219143947_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### O: OR logic operation of AND functions (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "OR logic operation of AND functions" to execute several AND logic operations before an OR logic operation. The overall result of the AND logic operations is saved temporarily and ORed with further signal queries.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/44600817931_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### A(: AND logic operation with branch (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "AND logic operation with branch" to execute the instructions of a parenthesized expression before an AND logic operation.

When the instruction executes, the CPU saves the current result of logic operation (RLO), as well as the binary result BR. The saved RLO is ANDed with the result of logic operation of the complete nested expression. If additional signal queries follow after the nested expression, these are also ANDed.

Parenthesized expressions can also be nested by programming an instruction within the parenthesized expression that also contains a parenthesized expression. The nesting depth is hereby limited to 7 levels.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19219283723_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### AN(: Negated AND logic operation with branch (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Negated AND logic operation with branch" instruction to execute the instructions of a parenthesized expression before an AND logic operation and to negate the complete result of the parenthesized expression.

When the instruction executes, the CPU saves the current result of logic operation (RLO), as well as the binary result BR. After the instructions in the parenthesized expression have executed, the RLO of the complete parenthesized expression is negated and ANDed with the saved RLO. If additional signal queries follow after the parenthesized expression, these are also ANDed.

Parenthesized expressions can also be nested by programming an instruction within the parenthesized expression that also contains a parenthesized expression. The nesting depth is hereby limited to 7 levels.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| AN( | // Start of the nested expression  // AND the RLO of the parenthesized expression and negate the complete result |
| O "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and OR with the current RLO. |
| O "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and OR with the current RLO. |
| ) | // End of the nested expression |
| AN "Tag_Input_3" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "0" and AND with the current RLO. |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign signal state of the RLO to the operand. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### O(: OR logic operation with branch (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "OR logic operation with branch" to execute the instructions of a parenthesized expression before an OR logic operation.

When the instruction executes, the CPU saves the current result of logic operation (RLO), as well as the binary result BR. After the instructions contained in the parenthesized expression have executed, the saved RLO is ORed with the RLO of the complete parenthesized expression. If additional signal queries follow after the parenthesized expression, these are also ORed.

Parenthesized expressions can also be nested by programming an instruction within the parenthesized expression that also contains a parenthesized expression. The nesting depth is hereby limited to 7 levels.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| O( | // Start of the nested expression  // OR the RLO of the nested expression |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_3" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| ) | // End of the nested expression |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign signal state of the RLO to the operand. |

---

#### ON(: Negated OR logic operation with branch (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Negated OR logic operation with branch" instruction to execute the instructions of a parenthesized expression before an OR logic operation and to negate the complete result of the parenthesized expression.

When the instruction executes, the CPU saves the current result of logic operation (RLO), as well as the binary result BR. After the instructions in the parenthesized expression have executed, the RLO of the complete parenthesized expression is negated and ORed with the saved RLO. If additional signal queries follow after the parenthesized expression, these are also ORed.

Parenthesized expressions can also be nested by programming an instruction within the parenthesized expression that also contains a parenthesized expression. The nesting depth is hereby limited to 7 levels.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| ON( | // Start of the nested expression  // Link RLO of the nested expression by OR logic and negate the complete result. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_3" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| ) | // End of the nested expression |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign signal state of the RLO to the operand. |

#### X(: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation with branch (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation with branch" to execute the instructions of a parenthesized expression before an EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation.

When the instruction executes, the CPU saves the current result of logic operation (RLO), as well as the binary result BR. After the instructions in the parenthesized expression have executed, the saved RLO is XORed with the RLO of the complete parenthesized expression. If additional signal queries follow after the parenthesized expression, these are also XORed.

Parenthesized expressions can also be nested by programming an instruction within the parenthesized expression that also contains a parenthesized expression. The nesting depth is hereby limited to 7 levels.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| X( | // Start of the nested expression  // Link RLO of the nested expression by EXCLUSIVE OR logic |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| ) | // End of the nested expression |
| X "Tag_Input_3" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign signal state of the RLO to the operand. |

[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### XN(: Negated EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation with branch (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Negated EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation with branch" instruction to execute the instructions of a parenthesized expression before an EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation and to negate the complete result of the parenthesized expression.

When the instruction executes, the CPU saves the current result of logic operation (RLO), as well as the binary result BR. After the instructions contained in the parenthesized expression have been executed, the RLO of the complete parenthesized expression will be negated and EXCLUSIVE ORed with the saved RLO. If additional signal queries follow after the parenthesized expression, these are also XORed.

Parenthesized expressions can also be nested by programming an instruction within the parenthesized expression that also contains a parenthesized expression. The nesting depth is hereby limited to 7 levels.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| XN( | // Start of the nested expression  // Link RLO of the nested expression by EXCLUSIVE OR logic and negate the complete result |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| ) | // End of the nested expression |
| XN "Tag_Input_3" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign signal state of the RLO to the operand. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-1500)

[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### ): Close branch (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Close branch" instruction to specify the end of a parenthesized expression. After processing of the instruction the complete result of the nested expression is linked according to the instruction that was used to open the nested expression.

Use the following instructions to open a nested expression:

- A(: AND logic operation with branch
- AN(: Negated AND logic operation with branch
- O(: OR logic operation with branch
- ON(: Negated OR logic operation with branch
- X(: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation with branch
- XN(: Negated EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation with branch

After the "Close branch" instruction, the CPU sets the binary result BR to the signal state that it had before the parenthesized expression.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19219283723_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### =: Assignment (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Assignment" instruction to assign the signal state of a result of logic operation (RLO) saved in the CPU to a specified operand. If the RLO has signal state "1", the operand is set. If the signal is "0", the operand is reset to "0".

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Assignment" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Operand to which the current RLO is assigned. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/19219444363_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### R: Reset (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Reset" instruction to reset the signal state of a specified operand to "0".

The instruction is only executed when the current result of logic operation (RLO) is "1". After execution of the instruction the specified operand is reset to "0". If there is a current RLO of "0", the signal state of the specified operand remains unchanged.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Reset" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Operand that is reset when RLO = "1". |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| R "Tag_Output" | // Reset the operand to "0" if RLO is "1" |

---

#### S: Set (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Set" instruction to set the signal state of a specified operand to "1".

The instruction is only executed when the current result of logic operation (RLO) is "1". After the instruction executes, the specified operand is set to "1". If there is a current RLO of "0", the signal state of the specified operand remains unchanged.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Set" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Operand that is set when RLO = "1". |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| S "Tag_Output" | // Sets the operand to "1" if RLO = "1". |

---

#### NOT: Invert RLO (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Invert RLO" instruction to invert the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). You can use the "Invert RLO" instruction anywhere, even within a logic operation.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the signal state of the "Tag_Input_1" operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the signal state of the "Tag_Input_2" operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| A "Tag_Input_3" | // Query the signal state of the "Tag_Input_3" operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| NOT | // Invert signal state of the RLO |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign signal state of the RLO to the "Tag_Output" operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input_1 | 1 | 1 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 |
| Tag_Input_2 | 0 | 1 | 1 | 0 | 1 | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Tag_Input_3 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | 1 |
| Tag_Output | 1 | 1 | 0 | 1 | 1 | 1 | 1 | 1 |

##### Description

Use the "Set RLO to 1" instruction to set the current result of logic operation (RLO) to signal state "1".

#### SAVE: Save RLO in BR bit (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Save RLO in BR bit" instruction to save the result of logic operation (RLO) in the binary result (BR). When it executes, the instruction transfers the signal state of the current result of logic operation to the status bit BR. The instruction operates independent of the conditions and does not affect any other status bits.

> **Note**
>
> After executing the "Save RLO in BR bit" instruction, the BR bit can be modified again by the following instructions in the same or lower-level blocks.

Use the "Save RLO in BR bit" instruction to check the execution status of a block. If, for example, you use the instruction "Save RLO in BR bit" at the end of a block, the BR bit is set to the signal state of the current result of logic operation of the block.

The BR bit helps to implement the EN/ENO mechanism for block calls. For more information on this topic, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input" | // Query signal state of the Tag_Input operand for "1". |
| SAVE | // Transfer signal state of the RLO to the BR bit. |
| BEC | // End of block if RLO = "1". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### FN: Scan RLO for negative signal edge (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Scan RLO for negative signal edge" instruction to query if a "1" to "0" change exists in the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The instruction compares the current signal state of the RLO with the signal state of the previous query saved in the edge memory bit (&lt;Operand&gt;). If the instruction detects a change in the RLO from "1" to "0", there is a negative signal edge.

The following figure shows the change in the RLO in case of a negative or positive signal edge:

![Description](images/83117930891_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The negative signal edge is queried each time the instruction executes. When a negative signal edge is detected, the RLO is set to signal state "1" for the length of one program cycle after the edge evaluation. In all other cases, the signal state of the RLO is "0".

> **Note**
>
> **Modification of the address of the edge memory bit**
>
> The address of the edge memory bit must not be used more than once in the program, otherwise the bit memory is overwritten. This step influences the edge evaluation and the result is therefore no longer unique. The memory area of the edge memory bit has to be located in a DB (static area for FB) or in the bit memory area.​

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Scan RLO for negative signal edge" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Edge memory bit in which the RLO of the previous query is saved. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/23336491019_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### FP: Scan RLO for positive signal edge (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Scan RLO for positive signal edge" instruction to query if a "0" to "1" change exists in the signal state of the result of logic operation (RLO). The instruction compares the current signal state of the RLO with the signal state of the previous query saved in the edge memory bit (&lt;Operand&gt;). If the instruction detects a change in the RLO from "0" to "1", there is a positive signal edge.

The following figure shows the change in the RLO in case of a negative or positive signal edge:

![Description](images/83117930891_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The positive signal edge is queried each time the instruction executes. When a positive signal edge is detected, the RLO is set to signal state "1" for the length of one program cycle after the edge evaluation. In all other cases, the signal state of the RLO is "0".

> **Note**
>
> **Modification of the address of the edge memory bit**
>
> The address of the edge memory bit must not be used more than once in the program, otherwise the bit memory is overwritten. This step influences the edge evaluation and the result is therefore no longer unique. The memory area of the edge memory bit has to be located in a DB (static area for FB) or in the bit memory area.​

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the instruction "Scan RLO for positive signal edge":

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Edge memory bit in which the RLO of the previous query is saved. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/23340680715_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

---

### Timer operations (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [FR: Enable timer (S7-1500)](#fr-enable-timer-s7-1500)
- [L: Load timer value (S7-1500)](#l-load-timer-value-s7-1500)
- [LC: Load BCD-coded timer value (S7-1500)](#lc-load-bcd-coded-timer-value-s7-1500)
- [R: Reset timer (S7-1500)](#r-reset-timer-s7-1500)
- [SP: Start pulse timer (S7-1500)](#sp-start-pulse-timer-s7-1500)
- [SE: Start extended pulse timer (S7-1500)](#se-start-extended-pulse-timer-s7-1500)
- [SD: Start on-delay timer (S7-1500)](#sd-start-on-delay-timer-s7-1500)
- [SS: Start retentive on-delay timer (S7-1500)](#ss-start-retentive-on-delay-timer-s7-1500)
- [SF: Start off-delay timer (S7-1500)](#sf-start-off-delay-timer-s7-1500)

#### FR: Enable timer (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "Enable timer" to restart a timer. The instruction is executed with a positive edge and resets the internal edge trigger flag for the starting of a timer. During the processing of an instruction for starting the timer with a result of logic operation "1", the timer restarts even if no positive signal edge is present before the start instruction. If the result of logic operation is "0" before a start instruction, the resetting of the internal edge trigger flag does not affect the timer.

A change of the result of logic operation to "0" before the "Enable timer" instruction has no affect after the restart of the timer.

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.

You can find an example of how a time cell can be formed under: See also "L: Load timer value".

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Enable timer" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Enabled timer |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_EnableInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| FR "MyTimer" | // If the signal edge is positive, enable timer. |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SP "MyTimer" | // Start pulse timer if there is a positive signal edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer. |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| L "MyTimer" | // Load current time value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-1500)
  
[L: Load timer value (S7-1500)](#l-load-timer-value-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### L: Load timer value (S7-1500)

##### Description

With the "Load timer value" instruction you load the timer value of a specified timer in accumulator 1. The dual-coded timer value is loaded without the timebase. Zeros are written to accumulator 1 instead of the timebase.

After the loading, the value in accumulator 1 corresponds to a positive number of the data type INT.

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.

The following figure is an example of how the time value is loaded in the accumulator:

![Description](images/19219784587_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Load timer value" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer whose current time value is loaded |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_EnableInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| FR "MyTimer" | // If edge is positive, enable timer. |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SP "MyTimer" | // Start timer as pulse if there is a positive edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer. |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| L "MyTimer" | // Load current time value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### LC: Load BCD-coded timer value (S7-1500)

##### Description

With the "Load BCD-coded timer value" instruction you load a BCD-coded timer value of a specified timer that exists dual coded in accumulator 1. During loading the timebase is also transferred to Accumulator 1.

After loading, the value in accumulator 1 corresponds to a time duration in S5TIME format. The left word in accumulator 1 is padded with zeros.

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.

The following figure shows how the time value is loaded in the accumulator:

![Description](images/44600813579_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

##### Parameters

The following table shows how the parameters of the "Load BCD-coded timer value" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer whose current BCD-coded timer value is loaded. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_EnableInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| FR "MyTimer" | // If edge is positive, enable timer. |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SP "MyTimer" | // Start timer as pulse if there is a positive edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer. |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| LC "MyTimer" | // Load current BCD-coded timer value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### R: Reset timer (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the "Reset timer" instruction to reset a specified timer to "0". The instruction is executed when the current result of logic operation (RLO) is "1". As long as the RLO is "1" before the instruction, the specified timer returns the value "0". The instruction also resets the time value and the time basis of the programmed period of time to "0".

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.

> **Note**
>
> The "Reset timer" instruction does not reset the internal edge memory bit. To reset the internal edge memory bit, program the "Enable timer" instruction or execute an instruction to start the time with the signal state "0".

You can find an example of how a time cell can be formed under: See also "L: Load timer value".

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Reset timer" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer, which is reset |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer. |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| L "MyTimer" | // Load current time value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-1500)

[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### SP: Start pulse timer (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the "Start pulse timer" instruction to start a specified timer on a positive signal edge. If a positive signal edge is detected, the instruction is executed and the timer started. The timer then runs down with the period of time specified in accumulator 1, as long as the result of logic operation (RLO) before the instruction remains "1". If the RLO changes to "0" before the end of the period of time, the timer is stopped. The queries of the timer status for "1" return the query result "1", as long as the period of time is running.

The timer can be restarted with a positive signal edge before the "Start pulse timer" instruction or using the "Enable timer" instruction. This restart can be effected provided the timer is not reset.

The period of time in accumulator 1 is made up of a time value and a time base. If a specified timer is started with the "Start pulse timer" instruction, the time value is counted down according to the timebase. The timer runs until the counter value is counted down to zero.

A valid period of time in S5TIME format must be present in accumulator 1, even if the timer is not started during the execution of the instruction. If the accumulator 1 does not include a valid BCD value and the RLO of the preceding logic operation returns the value "0", the status bit OV is set to "1". No synchronous error handling is started. If the accumulator 1 does include a valid BCD value, the status bit OV is reset to "0".

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.
>
> You can find an example of how a time cell can be formed under: See also "L: Load timer value".

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Start pulse timer" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer that is started as pulse. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SP "MyTimer" | // Start pulse timer if there is a positive signal edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer and stop timing |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| L "MyTimer" | // Load current time value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |
| LC "MyTimer" | // Load current time value in BCD format in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue_BCD" | // Transfer time value in BCD format to operand "Tag_TimerValue_BCD" |

The figure below shows the timer diagram of the example:

![Example](images/96174525707_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

---

#### SE: Start extended pulse timer (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the "Start extended pulse timer" to start a specified timer on a positive signal edge. If a positive signal edge is detected, the instruction is executed and the timer started. The timer then runs down with the period of time specified in accumulator 1, as long as the result of logic operation changes to "0" before the instruction. The queries of the timer status for "1" return the query result "1", as long as the period of time is running.

With each positive signal edge, the instruction restarts the timer with the programmed time duration, even if the timer has still not run down.

The period of time in accumulator 1 is made up of a time value and a time base. If a specified timer is started with the "Start extended pulse timer" instruction, the time value is counted down according to the timebase. The timer runs until the counter value is counted down to zero.

A valid period of time in S5TIME format must be present in accumulator 1, even if the timer is not started during the execution of the instruction. If the accumulator 1 does not include a valid BCD value and the RLO of the preceding logic operation returns the value "0", the status bit OV is set to "1". No synchronous error handling is started. If the accumulator 1 does include a valid BCD value, the status bit OV is reset to "0".

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.
>
> You can find an example of how a time cell can be formed here: [L: Load timer value](#l-load-timer-value-s7-1500)

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Start extended pulse timer" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer, which is started as extended pulse |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SE "MyTimer" | // Start timer as extended pulse if there is a positive signal edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer and stop timing |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| L "MyTimer" | // Load current time value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |
| LC "MyTimer" | // Load current time value in BCD format in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue_BCD" | // Transfer time value in BCD format to operand "Tag_TimerValue_BCD" |

#### SD: Start on-delay timer (S7-1500)

##### Description

The "Start on-delay timer" instruction starts a programmed timer when the signal state "1" is detected at the start input. As long as this signal state remains "1", the timer expires with the duration specified in accumulator 1. When the timer expires and the signal state at the start input is still "1", the query for timer status also returns "1". If the signal at the start input is "0", the timer is reset. In this case, querying the timer status returns the signal state "0". As soon as the signal at the start input changes to "1" again, the timer starts running again.

The signal state of the timer output is identical to the signal state of the start input. The start input is directly interconnected to the output and is not linked to the timer.

The duration in accumulator 1 is made up internally of a time value and a time base. When the instruction starts, the programmed time value counts down to zero.

A valid period of time in S5TIME format must be present in accumulator 1, even if the timer is not started during the execution of the instruction. If the accumulator 1 does not include a valid BCD value and the RLO of the preceding logic operation returns the value "0", the status bit OV is set to "1". No synchronous error handling is started. If the accumulator 1 does include a valid BCD value, the status bit OV is reset to "0".

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.
>
> You can find an example of how a time cell can be formed under: See also "L: Load timer value".

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Start on-delay timer" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer, which is started as on delay |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SD "MyTimer" | // Start timer as an on delay if there is a positive signal edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer and stop timing |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| L "MyTimer" | // Load current time value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |
| LC "MyTimer" | // Load current time value in BCD format in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue_BCD" | // Transfer time value in BCD format to the operand "Tag_TimerValue_BCD" |

The figure below shows the timer diagram of the example:

![Example](images/96204530699_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### SS: Start retentive on-delay timer (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the "Start retentive on-delay timer" instruction to start a specified timer on a positive signal edge. If a positive signal edge is detected, the instruction is executed and the timer started. The timer then runs with the period of time specified in accumulator 1, even if the result of logic operation (RLO) changes to "0" before the instruction. When the time has run out, queries of the timer status for "1" return the query result "1". The query result is not hereby affected by the signal state of the current result of logic operation before the instruction.

With each positive edge, the instruction restarts the timer with the programmed period of time, even if the time has still not run down.

The period of time in accumulator 1 is made up of a time value and a time base. If a specified timer is started with the "Start retentive on-delay timer" instruction, the time value is counted down according to the time base. The timer runs until the counter value is counted down to zero.

A valid period of time in S5TIME format must be present in accumulator 1, even if the timer is not started during the execution of the instruction. If the accumulator 1 does not include a valid BCD value and the RLO of the preceding logic operation returns the value "0", the status bit OV is set to "1". No synchronous error handling is started. If the accumulator 1 does include a valid BCD value, the status bit OV is reset to "0".

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.
>
> You can find an example of how a time cell can be formed here: [L: Load timer value](#l-load-timer-value-s7-1500)

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Start retentive on-delay timer" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer that is started as retentive on delay |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SS "MyTimer" | // Start retentive on-delay timer if there is a positive signal edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer and stop timing |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |
| = "Tag_TimerStatus" | // Assign timer status to the operand. |
| L "MyTimer" | // Load current time value of timer in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_TimerValue" | // Transfer current time value to operand "Tag_TimerValue". |

#### SF: Start off-delay timer (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the "Start off-delay timer" instruction to start a specified timer on a positive signal edge. If a negative signal edge is detected, the instruction is executed and the timer started. The timer then runs down with the period of time specified in accumulator 1. If the result of logic operation (RLO) changes to "1" before the end of the period of time, the timer is reset. The timer is only restarted if a negative signal edge is detected during the processing of the instruction.

The queries of the timer status for "1" return the query result "1" if the signal state of the result of logic operation is "1" at the execution of the instruction or if the programmed time is running. If the time does not elapse or the RLO is "0", queries of the timer status for "1" return the query result "0".

The period of time in accumulator 1 is made up of a time value and a time base. If a specified timer is started with the "Start off-delay timer" instruction, the time value is counted down according to the timebase. The timer runs until the counter value is counted down to zero.

A valid period of time in S5TIME format must be present in accumulator 1, even if the timer is not started during the execution of the instruction. If the accumulator 1 does not include a valid BCD value and the RLO of the preceding logic operation returns the value "0", the status bit OV is set to "1". No synchronous error handling is started. If the accumulator 1 does include a valid BCD value, the status bit OV is reset to "0".

> **Note**
>
> In the time cell, the operating system reduces the time value in an interval specified by the time base by one unit until the value equals "0". The decrementation is performed asynchronously to the user program. The resulting timer is therefore at maximum up to one time interval shorter than the desired time base.
>
> You can find an example of how a time cell can be formed here: [L: Load timer value](#l-load-timer-value-s7-1500)

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Start off-delay timer" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;timer&gt; | Input | TIMER | T | Timer, which is started as off delay |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_StartInput" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| L S5T#10s | // Load period of time (10s) |
| SF "MyTimer" | // Start timer as an off delay if there is a negative signal edge at the "Tag_StartInput" operand or at the "Tag_EnableInput" operand and the "Tag_StartInput" operand has signal state "1". |
| A "Tag_Reset" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| R "MyTimer" | // If RLO = "1", reset timer and stop timing |
| A "MyTimer" | // Query status of timer for "1". |

### Counter operations (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [FR: Enable counter (S7-1500)](#fr-enable-counter-s7-1500)
- [L: Load counter (S7-1500)](#l-load-counter-s7-1500)
- [LC: Load BCD-coded counter value (S7-1500)](#lc-load-bcd-coded-counter-value-s7-1500)
- [R: Reset counter (S7-1500)](#r-reset-counter-s7-1500)
- [S: Set counter (S7-1500)](#s-set-counter-s7-1500)
- [CU: Count up (S7-1500)](#cu-count-up-s7-1500)
- [CD: Count down (S7-1500)](#cd-count-down-s7-1500)

#### FR: Enable counter (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the "Enable counter" instruction to execute the instructions "Set counter", "Count up" and "Count down" without the presence of a positive signal edge. During processing, the instruction resets the internal edge flag to the signal state "0". The query before the corresponding count instruction must continue to have signal state "1".

The "Enable counter" instruction is executed when the result of logic operation (RLO) before the instruction changes from "0" to "1".

A counter does not have to be enabled for the count instruction to be executed.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Enable counter" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | COUNTER | C | Counter that is enabled. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query signal state for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| FR "MyCounter" | // Enable counter |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query signal state for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| CD "MyCounter" | // Count down |
| A "MyCounter" | // Query counter status |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign query result to the operand. |

In the example the counter ("MyCounter") is enabled when the signal state of the operand "Tag_Input_1" changes from "0" to "1". When the operand "Tag_Input_2" has signal state "1", the count value is decremented by one when the counter is enabled. When the signal state of the address "Tag_Input_2" is "0", the count value remains unchanged. The count value is also decremented by one regardless of the counter enabling, when the signal state of the address "Tag_Input_2" changes from "0" to "1".

The query of the counter status has the result "1" when the counter reading is greater than zero. If the counter reading is equal to zero, the result of the query is "0".

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### L: Load counter (S7-1500)

##### Description

With the "Load counter" instruction you transfer the current value of a specified counter in binary coding to the right word of accumulator 1. The loaded counter is then available as a 16-bit integer for additional processing.

The following figure shows how the instruction works:

![Description](images/19219734411_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Load counter" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | COUNTER | C | Counter whose current value is loaded. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "MyCounter" | // Load current counter value binary-coded in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Move the counter value to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;=I | // Query whether the count value is greater than or equal to the value of the address "Tag_Value" |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign query result to the operand. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### LC: Load BCD-coded counter value (S7-1500)

##### Description

With the "Load BCD-coded counter value" instruction you transfer the current value of a specified BCD-coded counter to the right word of accumulator 1. The loaded counter value is then available in BCD form for additional processing.

The following figure shows how the "Load BCD-coded counter value" instruction works:

![Description](images/20682593931_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Load BCD-coded counter value" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | COUNTER | C | Counter whose current value is loaded. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LC "MyCounter" | // Load current BCD-coded counter value in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer current counter value to the address "Tag_Output" and save. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
