##### CALL: Call block (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Call block" instruction to call the following block types in the program:

- Functions
- Function blocks

The "Call block" instruction executes without any conditions. After processing of the instruction, program execution is resumed in the called block.

You can feed a called block with data. The data is transferred via the block parameters. The parameters of the called block are listed according to the call instruction in the called block. You can assign the required current parameters to these parameters. During execution of the "Call block" instruction, the data is transferred to the called block. By transferring the data, the content of the status word and the address and data block registers are changed.

Those parameters of a function block that are not fed with parameters, retain their current value. All parameters must be fed when functions are called. If a called block has no parameters, no parameter list is displayed.

If the called block requires an instance data block, give it to the block, separated by a comma when called. The specified data block must be created before the call.

When the called block is processed, the CPU switches back to the calling block and resumes the processing of this block after the call instruction.

> **Note**
>
> The "Conditional block call" instruction can only be used when the block property "Parameter passing via registers" is disabled.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL "MyFunction"    Input_1 := "Tag_Input_1",   Input_2 := "Tag_Input_2"   Output_1 := "Tag_Output_1"   Output_2 := "Tag_Output_1" | // Call function "MyFunction"  // Assign actual parameters |
| CALL "MyFunctionBlock", "MyFB_DB"   Value_1 := "Tag_Value_1"   Value_2 := "Tag_Value_2"   Output := "Tag_Output" | // Call function block "MyFunctionBlock"  // Assign actual parameters |
| CALL "LIMIT"   MN := "Tag_LowLimit"   IN := "Tag_InputValue"   MX := "Tag_HighLimit"   OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Call "Set limit value" instruction  // Assign actual parameters |
| CALL "CTU", "CTU_DB"   CU := "Tag_StartCTU"   R := "Tag_ResetCounter"   PV := "Tag_PresetValue"   Q := "Tag_CounterStatus"   CV := "Tag_CounterValue" | // Call "Count up" counter  // Assign actual parameters |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### CC: Conditional block call (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Conditional block call" instruction to call functions (FCs) and function blocks (FBs) depending on the result of logic operation (RLO).

The instruction is only executed if the current result of logic operation (RLO) before execution of the instruction is "1". After processing of the instruction, program execution is resumed in the called block. When the called block is processed, the CPU switches back to the calling block and resumes the processing of this block after the call instruction.

If there is a block change, the status bit OS is reset to "0". The status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV are affected depending on the calling block.

> **Note**
>
> The "Conditional block call" instruction can only be used when the block property "Parameter passing via registers" is enabled. However, this lowers performance.

The contents of the accumulators and the address registers are not changed by the "Conditional block call" instruction.

If the current RLO is "0", the instruction as well as the block call are not executed and the RLO is set to "1".

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the value of operand "Tag_Input_1" for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| CC "MyFunction" | // If condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), call the function MyFunction.  // If the condition is not satisfied(RLO = "0"), execute the next instruction. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the value of operand "Tag_Input_2" for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| CC "MyFunctionBlock" | // If condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), call the function block MyFunctionBlock.  // If the condition is not satisfied(RLO = "0"), execute the next instruction. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

[Instances](Programming%20basics.md#instances)

[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)

##### UC: Unconditional block call (S7-1500)

###### Description

You can use the "Unconditional block call" instruction to call functions (FCs) and function blocks (FBs) that have no parameters and no instance data blocks.

The instruction is executed regardless of conditions. After processing of the instruction, program execution is resumed in the called block. When the called block is processed, the CPU switches back to the calling block and resumes the processing of this block after the call instruction.

If there is a block change, the status bit OS is reset to "0". The status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV are affected depending on the calling block.

> **Note**
>
> The "Unconditional block call" instruction can only be used when the block property "Parameter passing via registers" is enabled. However, this lowers performance.

The contents of the accumulators and the address registers are not changed by the "Unconditional block call" instruction.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query the value of operand "Tag_Input_1" for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| UC "MyFunction" | // Call function "MyFunction". |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query the value of operand "Tag_Input_2" for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| UC "MyFunctionBlock" | // Call function block "MyFunctionBlock". |

---

### Word logic operations (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [AW: AND logic operation word by word (S7-1500)](#aw-and-logic-operation-word-by-word-s7-1500)
- [OW: OR logic operation word by word (S7-1500)](#ow-or-logic-operation-word-by-word-s7-1500)
- [XOW: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation word by word (S7-1500)](#xow-exclusive-or-logic-operation-word-by-word-s7-1500)
- [AD: AND logic operation double word by double word (S7-1500)](#ad-and-logic-operation-double-word-by-double-word-s7-1500)
- [OD: OR logic operation double word by double word (S7-1500)](#od-or-logic-operation-double-word-by-double-word-s7-1500)
- [XOD: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation double word by double word (S7-1500)](#xod-exclusive-or-logic-operation-double-word-by-double-word-s7-1500)

#### AW: AND logic operation word by word (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "AND logic operation word by word" to AND the value of the right word in accumulator 1 with the value of the right word in accumulator 2 or a specified constant bit by bit. The result is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The contents of the left word in accumulator 1 remain unchanged.

The instruction links bit 0 of accumulator 1 with bit 0 of accumulator 2 or a constant and saves the result to bit 0 of accumulator 1. Bits 1 to 15 are linked in the same manner.

The result bit has signal state "1" if both of the bits in the logic operation also have signal state "1". If one of the two bits of the logic operation has signal state "0", the corresponding result bit is reset.

The following table shows how the result is formed by an AND word logic operation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 / constant | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 |
| Accumulator 1 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Result | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 |

The instruction is executed independent of conditions and does not affect the result of logic operation.

The instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "AND logic operation word by word" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | WORD | Value that is ANDed with the value in the right word of accumulator 1. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| AW W#16#F6B5 | // AND the value of the right word in accumulator 1 with the constant (W#16#F6B5).  // Save the result in the right word of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| AW | // AND the value of the right word in accumulator 2 ("Tag_Value_2") with the value of the right word in accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3")   // Save the result in the right word of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_2". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1001 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Constant (W#16#F6B5) | 1111 | 0110 | 1011 | 0101 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0101 | 0000 | 0011 | 0001 |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0110 | 1100 | 0010 | 1010 |
| Tag_Value_3 | 1101 | 1010 | 1001 | 0011 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0100 | 1000 | 0000 | 0010 |

---

#### OW: OR logic operation word by word (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "OR logic operation word by word" to OR the value of the right word in accumulator 1 with the value of the right word in accumulator 2 or a specified constant bit by bit. The result is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The contents of the left word in accumulator 1 remain unchanged.

The instruction links bit 0 of accumulator 1 with bit 0 of accumulator 2 or a constant and saves the result to bit 0 of accumulator 1. Bits 1 to 15 are linked in the same manner.

The result bit has signal state "1" when at least one of the two bits in the logic operation has signal state "1". If both bits of the logic operation have signal state "0", the corresponding result bit is reset to "0".

The following table shows how the result is formed by an OR word logic operation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 / constant | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 |
| Accumulator 1 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Result | 0 | 1 | 1 | 1 |

The instruction is executed independent of conditions and does not affect the result of logic operation.

The instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "OR logic operation word by word" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | WORD | Value that is ORed with the value in the right word of accumulator 1. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| OW W#16#F6B5 | // OR the value of the right word in accumulator 1 with the constant (W#16#F6B5).  // Save the result in the right word of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| OW | // OR the value of the right word in accumulator 2 ("Tag_Value_2") with the value of the right word in accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3")  // Save the result in the right word of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_2". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1001 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Constant (W#16#F6B5) | 1111 | 0110 | 1011 | 0101 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 1111 | 1111 | 1011 | 1111 |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0110 | 1100 | 0010 | 1010 |
| Tag_Value_3 | 1101 | 1010 | 1001 | 0011 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 1111 | 1110 | 1011 | 1011 |

#### XOW: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation word by word (S7-1500)

##### Description

Use the instruction "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation word by word" to EXCLUSIVE OR the value of the right word in accumulator 1 with the value of the right word in accumulator 2 or a specified constant bit by bit. The result is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The contents of the left word in accumulator 1 remain unchanged.

The instruction links bit 0 of accumulator 1 with bit 0 of accumulator 2 or a constant and saves the result to bit 0 of accumulator 1. Bits 1 to 15 are linked in the same manner.

The result bit has signal state "1" if the signal state of the two bits to be linked is different. If both of the bits of the logic operation have the same signal state, the corresponding result bit is reset to "0".

The following table shows how the result is formed by an EXCLUSIVE OR word logic operation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 / constant | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 |
| Accumulator 1 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Result | 0 | 1 | 1 | 0 |

The instruction is executed independent of conditions and does not affect the result of logic operation.

The instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation word by word" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | WORD | Value that is XORed with the value in the right word of accumulator 1. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| XOW W#16#F6B5 | // XOR the value of the right word in accumulator 1 with the constant (W#16#F6B5).  // Save the result in the right word of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| XOW | // XOR the value of the right word in accumulator 2 ("Tag_Value_2") with the value of the right word in accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3")  // Save the result in the right word of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_2". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1001 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Constant (W#16#F6B5) | 1111 | 0110 | 1011 | 0101 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 1010 | 1111 | 1000 | 1110 |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0110 | 1100 | 0010 | 1010 |
| Tag_Value_3 | 1101 | 1010 | 1001 | 0011 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 1011 | 0110 | 1011 | 1001 |

#### AD: AND logic operation double word by double word (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the instruction "AND logic operation double word by double word" to AND the contents of accumulator 1 with the contents of accumulator 2 or with the value of a specified constant, bit by bit. The result is stored in accumulator 1.

The instruction links bit 0 of accumulator 1 with bit 0 of accumulator 2 or a constant and saves the result to bit 0 of accumulator 1. Bits 1 to 31 are linked in the same manner.

The result bit has signal state "1" if both of the bits in the logic operation also have signal state "1". If one of the two bits of the logic operation has signal state "0", the corresponding result bit is reset.

The following table shows how the result is formed by an AND word logic operation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 / constant | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 |
| Accumulator 1 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Result | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 |

The instruction is executed independent of conditions and does not affect the result of logic operation.

The instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the instruction "AND logic operation double word by double word":

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | DWORD | Value that is ANDed with the value in accumulator 1. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand into accumulator 1. |
| AD DW#16#39C657AC | // AND the value in accumulator 1 with the constant (DW#16#39C657AC).  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand into accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1. |
| AD | // AND the value of accumulator 2 Tag_Value_2 with the value of accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3")  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_2". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 1001 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Constant (DW#16#39C657AC) | 0011 | 1001 | 1100 | 0110 | 0101 | 0111 | 1010 | 1100 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0001 | 1001 | 0100 | 0100 | 0001 | 0101 | 0010 | 1000 |
|  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0110 | 0101 | 0100 | 0011 | 0101 | 1101 | 0010 | 1011 |
| Tag_Value_3 | 0011 | 1001 | 1100 | 0110 | 0101 | 0111 | 1010 | 1100 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0010 | 0001 | 0100 | 0010 | 0101 | 0101 | 0010 | 1010 |

---

#### OD: OR logic operation double word by double word (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the instruction "OR logic operation double word by double word" to OR the contents of accumulator 1 with the contents of accumulator 2 or with the value of a specified constant, bit by bit. The result is stored in accumulator 1.

The instruction links bit 0 of accumulator 1 with bit 0 of accumulator 2 or a constant and saves the result to bit 0 of accumulator 1. Bits 1 to 31 are linked in the same manner.

The result bit has signal state "1" when at least one of the two bits in the logic operation has signal state "1". If both bits of the logic operation have signal state "0", the corresponding result bit is reset to "0".

The following table shows how the result is formed by an OR word logic operation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 / constant | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 |
| Accumulator 1 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Result | 0 | 1 | 1 | 1 |

The instruction is executed independent of conditions and does not affect the result of logic operation.

The instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "OR logic operation double word by double word" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | DWORD | Value that is ORed with the value in accumulator 1. |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand into accumulator 1. |
| OD DW#16#39C657AC | // OR the value in accumulator 1 with the constant (DW#16#39C657AC).  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand into accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1. |
| OD | // OR the value of accumulator 2 Tag_Value_2 with the value of accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3")  // Store result in accumulator 1 |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_2". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 1001 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Constant (DW#16#39C657AC) | 0011 | 1001 | 1100 | 0110 | 0101 | 0111 | 1010 | 1100 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0111 | 1111 | 1110 | 0110 | 1101 | 1111 | 1011 | 1111 |
|  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0110 | 0101 | 0100 | 0011 | 0101 | 1101 | 0010 | 1011 |
| Tag_Value_3 | 0011 | 1001 | 1100 | 0110 | 0101 | 0111 | 1010 | 1100 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0111 | 1101 | 1100 | 0111 | 0101 | 1111 | 1110 | 1111 |

---

#### XOD: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation double word by double word (S7-1500)

##### Description

You can use the instruction "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation double word by double word" to XOR the contents of accumulator 1 with the contents of accumulator 2 bit by bit. The result is stored in accumulator 1.

The instruction links bit 0 of accumulator 1 with bit 0 of accumulator 2 or a constant and saves the result to bit 0 of accumulator 1. Bits 1 to 31 are linked in the same manner.

The result bit has signal state "1" if the signal state of the two bits to be linked is different. If both of the bits of the logic operation have the same signal state, the corresponding result bit is reset to "0".

The following table shows how the result is formed by an EXCLUSIVE OR word logic operation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 / constant | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 |
| Accumulator 1 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Result | 0 | 1 | 1 | 0 |

The instruction is executed independent of conditions and does not affect the result of logic operation.

The instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1 and OV.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation double word by double word" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | DWORD | Value that is XORed with the value in accumulator 1 |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand into accumulator 1. |
| XOD DW#16#39C657AC | // XOR the value in accumulator 1 with the constant (DW#16#39C657AC).  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand into accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1. |
| XOD | // XOR the value of accumulator 2 Tag_Value_2 with the value of accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3")  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_2". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 1001 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Constant (DW#16#39C657AC) | 0011 | 1001 | 1100 | 0110 | 0101 | 0111 | 1010 | 1100 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0110 | 0110 | 1010 | 0010 | 1100 | 1010 | 1001 | 0111 |
|  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0110 | 0101 | 0100 | 0011 | 0101 | 1101 | 0010 | 1011 |
| Tag_Value_3 | 0011 | 1001 | 1100 | 0110 | 0101 | 0111 | 1010 | 1100 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0101 | 1100 | 1000 | 0101 | 0000 | 1010 | 1000 | 0111 |

---

### Shift and rotate (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [Shift (S7-1500)](#shift-s7-1500)
- [Rotate (S7-1500)](#rotate-s7-1500)

#### Shift (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [SSI: Shift word by word with sign (S7-1500)](#ssi-shift-word-by-word-with-sign-s7-1500)
- [SSD: Shift double word by double word with sign (S7-1500)](#ssd-shift-double-word-by-double-word-with-sign-s7-1500)
- [SLW: Shift left word by word (S7-1500)](#slw-shift-left-word-by-word-s7-1500)
- [SRW: Shift right word by word (S7-1500)](#srw-shift-right-word-by-word-s7-1500)
- [SLD: Shift left double word by double word (S7-1500)](#sld-shift-left-double-word-by-double-word-s7-1500)
- [SRD: Shift right double word by double word (S7-1500)](#srd-shift-right-double-word-by-double-word-s7-1500)

##### SSI: Shift word by word with sign (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Shift word by word with sign" to shift the right word (bits 0 to 15) of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the right. During the shifting, positions that become free are padded with the signal state of bit 15 (sign bit for INT numbers). The bits 16 to 31 of accumulator 1 remain unchanged. The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be shifted:

- Specification of a positive integer as parameter of the instruction. (&lt;number&gt;).
- Specification via the value of the right byte in accumulator 2: The byte is interpreted as a positive integer.

You can use the following formats:

- SSI &lt;number&gt;: The number of shifts is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 15 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- SSI: The number of shifts is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  If the specified number of places shifted is greater than 15, all bits in the right word of accumulator 1 are padded with the signal state of bit 15.

If the specified number of places shifted is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers:   SINT, INT, UINT, USINT | Number of bit places by which the value will be shifted. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SSI 6 | // Shift bits 0 to 15 of accumulator 1 six places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with the state of bit 15. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| L 3 | // Load number of places shifted into accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places shifted to the right byte of accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SSI | // Shift bits 0 to 15 of accumulator 1 three places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with the state of bit 15. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 1001 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 1111 | 1110 | 0111 | 0100 |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0010 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0000 | 1011 | 1010 | 0101 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

##### SSD: Shift double word by double word with sign (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Shift double word by double word with sign" to shift the complete contents of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the right. During the shifting, positions that become free are padded with the signal state of bit 31 (sign bit for DINT numbers). The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be shifted:

- Specification of a positive integer as parameter of the instruction. (&lt;number&gt;).
- Specification via the value of the right byte in accumulator 2: The byte is interpreted as a positive integer.

You can use the following formats:

- SSD &lt;number&gt;: The number of shifts is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 31 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- SSD: The number of shifts is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  For values greater than 31, all bits of accumulator 1 are padded with the signal state of bit 31.

If the specified number of places shifted is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the instruction "Shift double word by double word with sign":

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers:   SINT, INT, UINT, USINT, | Number of bit places by which the value will be shifted. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SSD 7 | // Shift bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 seven places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with the state of bit 31. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| L 4 | // Load number of places shifted into accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places shifted to the right byte of accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SSD | // Shift bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 four places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with the state of bit 31. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 1000 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 1111 | 1111 | 0001 | 1110 | 1100 | 1000 | 1011 | 1010 |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 1100 | 1101 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0000 | 0010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 1100 |

---

##### SLW: Shift left word by word (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Shift left word by word" instruction to shift the right word (bits 0 to 15) of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the left. The bit places that become free are padded with zeros. The bits 16 to 31 of accumulator 1 remain unchanged. The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be shifted:

- Specification of a positive integer as parameter of the instruction. (&lt;number&gt;).
- Specification via the value of the right byte in accumulator 2: The byte is interpreted as a positive integer.

You can use the following formats:

- SLW &lt;Number&gt;: The number of shifts is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 15 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- SLW: The number of shifts is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  If the specified number of places shifted is greater than 15, all bits in the right word of accumulator 1 are padded with zeros.

If the specified number of places shifted is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Shift left word by word" instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers: SINT, INT, UINT, USINT | Number of bit places by which the value will be shifted. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SLW 5 | // Shift bits 0 to 15 of accumulator 1 five places to the left.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| L 4 | // Load number of places shifted into accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places shifted to the right byte of accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SLW | // Shift bits 0 to 15 of accumulator 1 four places to the left.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 1010 | 0111 | 0110 | 0000 |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0010 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 1101 | 0010 | 1011 | 0000 |

---

##### SRW: Shift right word by word (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Shift right word by word" instruction to shift the right word (bits 0 to 15) of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the right. The bit places that become free are padded with zeros. The bits 16 to 31 of accumulator 1 remain unchanged. The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be shifted:

- Specification of a positive integer as parameter of the instruction. (&lt;number&gt;).
- Specification via the value of the right byte in accumulator 2: The byte is interpreted as a positive integer.

You can use the following formats:

- SRW &lt;Number&gt;: The number of shifts is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 15 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- SRW: The number of shifts is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  If the specified number of places shifted is greater than 15, all bits in the right word of accumulator 1 are padded with zeros.

If the specified number of places shifted is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Shift right word by word" instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers: SINT, INT, UINT, USINT | Number of bit places by which the value will be shifted. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SRW 6 | // Shift bits 0 to 15 of accumulator 1 six places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| L 4 | // Load number of places shifted into accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places shifted to the right byte of accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SRW | // Shift bits 0 to 15 of accumulator 1 four places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0000 | 0001 | 0111 | 0100 |
| Tag_Value_2 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0010 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0000 | 0101 | 1101 | 0010 |

##### SLD: Shift left double word by double word (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Shift left double word by double word" instruction to shift the complete contents of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the left. The bit places that become free are padded with zeros. The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be shifted:

- SLD &lt;number&gt;: The number of shifts is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 31 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- SLD: The number of shifts is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  For values greater than 31, all bits of accumulator 1 are padded with zeros.

If the specified number of places shifted is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Shift left double word by double word" instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers: SINT, INT, UINT, USINT | Number of bit places by which the value will be shifted. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SLD 5 | // Shift bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 five places to the left.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places shifted to the right byte of accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SLD | // Shift bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 four places to the left.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 1110 | 1100 | 1000 | 1011 | 1010 | 0111 | 0110 | 0000 |
| Tag_Value_2 | 1010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 1100 | 1101 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 1000 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 1100 | 1101 | 0000 |

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Querying and setting status bits in STL (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-and-setting-status-bits-in-stl-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### SRD: Shift right double word by double word (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Shift right double word by double word" to shift the complete contents of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the right. The bit places that become free are padded with zeros. The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be shifted:

- Specification of a positive integer as parameter of the instruction. (&lt;number&gt;).
- Specification via the value of the right byte in accumulator 2: The byte is interpreted as a positive integer.

You can use the following formats:

- SRD &lt;number&gt;: The number of shifts is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 31 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- SRD: The number of shifts is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  For values greater than 31, all bits of accumulator 1 are padded with zeros.

If the specified number of places shifted is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Shift right double word by double word" instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers: SINT, INT, UINT, USINT | Number of bit places by which the value will be shifted. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SRD 7 | // Shift bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 seven places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| L 4 | // Load number of places shifted into accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places shifted to the right byte of accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| SRD | // Shift bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 four places to the right.  // Fill the now empty bit places with zeros. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 0000 | 0000 | 1011 | 1110 | 1100 | 1000 | 1011 | 1010 |
| Tag_Value_2 | 1010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 1100 | 1101 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0000 | 1010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 1100 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Querying and setting status bits in STL (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-and-setting-status-bits-in-stl-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)

#### Rotate (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [RLD: Rotate left double word by double word (S7-1500)](#rld-rotate-left-double-word-by-double-word-s7-1500)
- [RRD: Rotate right double word by double word (S7-1500)](#rrd-rotate-right-double-word-by-double-word-s7-1500)
- [RLDA: Rotate left by status bit CC 1 (S7-1500)](#rlda-rotate-left-by-status-bit-cc-1-s7-1500)
- [RRDA: Rotate right by status bit CC 1 (S7-1500)](#rrda-rotate-right-by-status-bit-cc-1-s7-1500)

##### RLD: Rotate left double word by double word (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Rotate left double word by double word" instruction to rotate the complete contents of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the left. During processing the instruction shifts bit 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the left and pads the places that become free during writing with the pushed out bit places. The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be rotated:

- Specification of a positive integer as parameter of the instruction. (&lt;number&gt;).
- Specification via the value of the right byte in accumulator 2: The byte is interpreted as a positive integer.

You can use the following formats:

- RLD &lt;number&gt;: The number of rotations is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 32 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- RLD: The number of rotations is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  For values greater than 32, the rotation number is calculated with a modulo division by 32. If, for example, the rotate number is 34, the bits of accumulator 1 are rotated by 2 bit places.

If the specified rotate number is 32, the contents of accumulator 1 remain unchanged.

If the specified rotate number is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Rotate left double word by double word" instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers: SINT, INT, UINT, USINT | Number of bit places to be rotated. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| RLD 4 | // Rotate bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 four places to the left |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| L 6 | // Load number of places to be rotated in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places to be rotated to right byte of accumulator 2  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| RLD | // Rotate bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 six places to the left |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | **0101** | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result_1 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 | **0101** |
| Tag_Value_2 | **1010** | **10**00 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 1100 | 1101 |
| Tag_Result_2 | 0010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0110 | 1111 | 0011 | 01**10** | **1010** |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Querying and setting status bits in STL (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-and-setting-status-bits-in-stl-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)

##### RRD: Rotate right double word by double word (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Rotate right double word by double word" instruction to rotate the complete contents of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the right. During processing the instruction shifts bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 bit by bit to the right and pads the places that become free during writing with the pushed out bit places. The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. The status bit CC1 is set to the signal state of the last bit that was shifted out.

The following options are available for specifying the number of bit places by which the bits are to be rotated:

- Specification of a positive integer as parameter of the instruction. (&lt;number&gt;).
- Specification via the value of the right byte in accumulator 2: The byte is interpreted as a positive integer.

You can use the following formats:

- RRD &lt;number&gt;: The number of rotations is specified by the operand &lt;number&gt;. Values between 0 and 32 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the &lt;number&gt; is greater than zero.
- RRD: The number of rotations is specified by the value in accumulator 2. Values between 0 and 255 are permitted. The status bits CC 0 and OV are reset to "0" when the content of accumulator 2 is greater than zero.

  For values greater than 32, the rotation number is calculated with a modulo division by 32. If, for example, the rotate number is 34, the bits of accumulator 1 are rotated by 2 bit places.

If the specified rotate number is 32, the contents of accumulator 1 remain unchanged.

If the specified rotate number is equal to zero, the instruction is still executed. The status bit CC1 is set to "0".

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the instruction "Rotate right double word by double word":

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Number&gt; | Positive integers: SINT, INT, UINT, USINT | Number of bit places to be rotated. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| RRD 4 | // Rotate bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 four places to the right. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| L 6 | // Load number of places to be rotated in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move number of places to be rotated to right byte of accumulator 2  // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| RRD | // Rotate bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 six places to the right. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value_1 | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | **1011** |
| Tag_Result_1 | **1011** | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 |
| Tag_Value_2 | 1010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0010 | 1001 | 1011 | 11**00** | **1101** |
| Tag_Result_2 | **0011** | **01**10 | 1010 | 0010 | 1000 | 1010 | 0110 | 1111 |

---

##### RLDA: Rotate left by status bit CC 1 (S7-1500)

###### Description

You can use the "Rotate left by status bit CC 1" instruction to shift the contents of accumulator 1 one bit to the left. The bit places (0) that become free during shifting are padded with the signal state of status bit CC 1. Status bit CC 1 receives the signal state of the shifted out bit (31).

The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. It resets the status bit CC 0 to "0".

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| RLDA | // Rotate bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 one place to the left  // Fill bit 0 with the signal state of status bit CC 1.  // Write the shifted-out bit to the status bit CC 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | CC 1 | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value | **1** | **0**101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result | **0** | 1011 | 1110 | 1100 | 1000 | 1011 | 1010 | 0111 | 011**1** |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Querying and setting status bits in STL (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-and-setting-status-bits-in-stl-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### RRDA: Rotate right by status bit CC 1 (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the "Rotate right by status bit CC 1" instruction to shift the contents of accumulator 1 one bit to the right. The bit places (31) that become free during shifting are padded with the signal state of status bit CC 1. Status bit CC 1 receives the signal state of the shifted out bit (0).

The instruction is executed regardless of the RLO. It resets the status bits CC0 and OV to "0".

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| RRDA | // Rotate bits 0 to 31 of accumulator 1 one place to the right  // Fill bit 31 with the signal state of status bit CC 1.  // Write the shifted-out bit to the status bit CC 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | CC 1 | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Value | **1** | **0**101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1011 |
| Tag_Result | **0** | **1**010 | 1111 | 1011 | 0010 | 0010 | 1110 | 1001 | 1101 |

Status bit CC 1 has the value "1" because the bit 0 of the "Tag_Value" operand also has the value "1".

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

### Additional instructions (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [Accumulator (S7-1500)](#accumulator-s7-1500)

- [Null instructions (S7-1500)](#null-instructions-s7-1500)

#### Accumulator (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [TAK: Swap content of accumulators 1 and 2 (S7-1500)](#tak-swap-content-of-accumulators-1-and-2-s7-1500)
- [PUSH: Shift content to the next higher accumulator (S7-1500)](#push-shift-content-to-the-next-higher-accumulator-s7-1500)
- [POP: Shift content to the next lower accumulator (S7-1500)](#pop-shift-content-to-the-next-lower-accumulator-s7-1500)

##### TAK: Swap content of accumulators 1 and 2 (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Swap content of accumulators 1 and 2" to switch the contents accumulator 1 with the contents of accumulator 2.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| JC NEXT | // If condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), jump to jump label NEXT.  // If the condition is not satisfied (RLO = "0"), execute the next instruction. |
| TAK | // Swap the contents of accumulators 1 and 2. |
| NEXT: -I | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Subtract value of accumulator 1 from value of accumulator 2. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Output". |

---

##### PUSH: Shift content to the next higher accumulator (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Shift content to the next higher accumulator" to move the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.

The content of accumulator 1 is not influenced by the instruction and remains unchanged after processing the instruction. The content of accumulator 2 will be lost.

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 to 2 before and after the executing the instruction:

| Status | Accumulator |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 2 |  |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B |
| After processing | Value A | Value A |

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| PUSH | // Shift contents of accumulators 1 to 2 to the next higher accumulator. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-1500)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-1500)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Instances](Programming%20basics.md#instances)

[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)

##### POP: Shift content to the next lower accumulator (S7-1500)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Shift content to the next lower accumulator" to move the contents of accumulator 2 to accumulator 1.

The content of accumulator 2 is not influenced by the instruction and remains unchanged after processing the instruction. The content of accumulator 1 will be lost.

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 to 2 before and after the executing the instruction:

| Status | Accumulator |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 2 |  |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B |
| After processing | Value B | Value B |

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| T "Tag_Value_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| POP | // Shift the contents of accumulator 2 to lower-order accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Value_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Value_2". |

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### Address register (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [+AR1: Add accumulator 1 to AR1 (S7-1500)](#ar1-add-accumulator-1-to-ar1-s7-1500)
- [+AR2: Add accumulator 1 to AR2 (S7-1500)](#ar2-add-accumulator-1-to-ar2-s7-1500)

##### +AR1: Add accumulator 1 to AR1 (S7-1500)

###### Description

With the "Add accumulator 1 to AR1" instruction you add a value to the content of address register 1. The type of pointer located in address register 1 and the operand range remain as they are.

The following options are available for specifying the value to be added:

- Specification via a constant: The instruction adds the value of the constant to address register 1. The value of the constant must correspond to the format of a range-internal pointer (POINTER).
- Specification via the value of the right word in the accumulator 1: The instruction interprets the value of the right word in accumulator 1 as a 16-bit integer and extends it with the correct sign to 24 bits. The instruction then adds value of accumulator 1 to address register 1. Values from -32768 to +32767 are permitted.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Add accumulator 1 to AR1" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | POINTER | Value that is added to address register 1. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| +AR1 P#10.0 | // Add pointer to address register 1. |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value" into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| +AR1 | // Add value of accumulator 1 to address register 1. |
| TAR1 %MD24 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to double word MD24. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Memory areas (S7-1500)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-1500%20CPUs%20%28S7-1500%29.md#memory-areas-s7-1500)

##### +AR2: Add accumulator 1 to AR2 (S7-1500)

###### Description

With the "Add accumulator 1 to AR2" instruction you add a value to the content of address register 2. The type of pointer located in address register 2 and the operand range remain as they are.

The following options are available for specifying the value to be added:

- Specification via a constant: The instruction adds the value of the constant to address register 2. The value of the constant must correspond to the format of a range-internal pointer (POINTER).
- Specification via the value of the right word in the accumulator 1: The instruction interprets the value of the right word in accumulator 1 as a 16-bit integer and extends it with the correct sign to 24 bits. The instruction then adds value of accumulator 1 to address register 2. Values from -32768 to +32767 are permitted.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

> **Note**
>
> Address register AR2 is used when processing multi-instances. If you program the "Add accumulator 1 to AR2" instruction, you must first "save" the contents of address register 2 and reload it later.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Add accumulator 1 to AR2" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | POINTER | Value that is added to address register 1. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| +AR2 P#10.0 | // Add pointer to address register 2. |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value" into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| +AR2 | // Add value of accumulator 1 to address register 2. |
| TAR2 %MD24 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to double word MD24. |

---

#### Null instructions (S7-1500)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [BLD: Program display (null instruction) (S7-1500)](#bld-program-display-null-instruction-s7-1500)
- [NOP 0: Null instruction (S7-1500)](#nop-0-null-instruction-s7-1500)
- [NOP 1: Null instruction (S7-1500)](#nop-1-null-instruction-s7-1500)

##### BLD: Program display (null instruction) (S7-1500)

###### Description

The instruction "Program display (null instruction)" does not execute any function and does not affect the status bits. The instruction is used to recognize code sequences during a parameter transfer or with LAD/FBD networks. It is created automatically when a LAD or FBD program is displayed in STL. The parameter value is the number of the instruction and is generated by the programming device.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Program display (null instruction)" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;number&gt; | WORD | Number of the instruction |

---

##### NOP 0: Null instruction (S7-1500)

###### Description

If "Null instruction" has a parameter 0, it does not execute any function and does not affect the status bits. The instruction code contains a bit pattern with 16 zeros. The instruction is only relevant for the programming device when a program is displayed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| A | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| JC NEXT | // If condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), jump to jump label NEXT.  // If the condition is not satisfied (RLO = "0"), execute the next instruction. |
| TAK | // Swap the contents of accumulators 1 and 2. |
| NEXT: NOP 0 | // Jump label "NEXT" |

---

##### NOP 1: Null instruction (S7-1500)

###### Description

If "Null instruction" has a parameter 1, it does not execute any function and does not affect the status bits. The instruction code contains a bit pattern with 16 ones. The instruction is only relevant for the programming device when a program is displayed.
